    <li> My Experience:  I have had my Oral B 5000 for about a year now.  I was going to review it soon after I bought it, but decided to wait because in my opinion, the real worth of a toothbrush of this nature is shown after using if for quite a while.  Let me just tell you, it works just as good now as it did the day I bought it.  I have extremely sensitive teeth and going to the dentist used to hurt due to all the scraping they had to do on my teeth.  Since I have been using this brush, I have had two cleanings and both times they did minimal scraping and it was actually a pleasant experience.  My teeth are so much whiter and my whole mouth really just feels better!  I buy my brush heads on Amazon for about half the price than what other stores offer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Clock:  I didn&#x27;t think I would use this feature as much as I do.  I mounted it to my bathroom mirror when I got it using the tape that is so conveniently provided.  I use it on a daily basis to keep up with time as I get ready for the day.  The pressure feature on the clock is amazing! I never realized that I brushed too hard and this thing has really gotten me into better brushing habits.  My favorite part, if you brush for 2:30 the smiley face winks at you. ;)  Since I have had the toothbrush, I have only changed the battery in the clock one time.  It has a battery meter on the front to let you know when it&#x27;s getting low.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Battery:  When it was brand new, the battery lasted ~10 days as advertised.  Now (roughly 12 months later), the batter lasts about half that time.  It&#x27;s really not that big of a deal to me because I store my toothbrush on the dock anyway, so I just have to plug it in a little more often.  The battery display on the toothbrush is always extremely accurate and lets me know right when I need to plug it in.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:  The carrying case is perfect - I love that it holds multiple brush heads.  The power cord has a piece of Velcro attached to it for easy storage.  The toothbrush head tray has a cover that folds down to keep dust and other random things off it it; this is wonderful for my inner germophobe.  The tray the brush heads sit in is also angled down so that any extra water doesn&#x27;t just sit on the bristles and they dry much faster.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:  The only thing I could possibly say negatively about this toothbrush is the lack of instruction that comes with it.  While brushing your teeth is by no means rocket science, this toothbrush has tons of fantastic features and it would be very helpful if someone told you how to do it.  I figured it out after toying with it for a while, but I shouldn&#x27;t have to do that when paying $150 for a toothbrush (thankfully, it has come down in price since I purchased).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I hope this helps.     <li> My husband and I purchased two Oral-B Professional Healthy Clean + Floss Action Precision 5000 Rechargeable Electric Toothbrushes and couldn&#x27;t be happier.  We use the floss action and pro-white brushing heads.  We&#x27;ve tried many toothbrushes over the years, including the expensive one the dentist insisted we needed to purchase because my husband suffers from gum disease.  None of the toothbrushes we&#x27;ve ever used can even come close to the cleaning power of this toothbrush.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have always been lectured from dentists for brushing too hard in one particular location - where I always start brushing first.  They said it&#x27;s because I have more energy when I start and am more aggressive.  This has caused my gum to recede down from my teeth in that spot.  I have had to have enamel replaced in that location twice.  Now that I use this brush, it will never be a problem again.  You don&#x27;t apply any pressure and you don&#x27;t use any brushing motion.  The toothbrush does ALL the work for you.  You just move from tooth to tooth slowly for perfectly clean teeth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let&#x27;s be honest, everyone at one time or another has eaten something and then immediately brushed their teeth only to feel that there are some residual food particles in and between their teeth.  Well, not with this brush.  The power of those 40,000 pulsations per minute and 8,800 oscillations per minute will get out even the most stubborn particles.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We have always brushed for about five minutes with other brushes and actually balked at the two minute brushing time recommended with this brush.  Well, truth be told, our teeth and gums look and feel much cleaner with two minutes of use with this brush than five minutes with any other brush.  You actually feel like you just had your teeth cleaned at the dentist every time you brush! I&#x27;m not kidding. We also notice our teeth are getting whiter without any special treatment or whitening toothpaste.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The unit has five brushing modes to choose from (Daily Clean, Deep Clean, Sensitive, Whitening, and Massage) and even tells you when you&#x27;re brushing too hard.  My husband came rushing out of the bathroom this morning to inform me that the unit gave him a sad face because he was brushing too hard.  LOL  The first few brushes it was a little difficult getting used to timed brushing by quadrant, but now I couldn&#x27;t brush any other way.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The smart guide (battery operated electric device you can mount on the wall that times you, lets you see what settings you&#x27;re using, which quadrant you&#x27;re supposed to be on, etc.) that comes with each brush can be programmed easily for two different brushes, which is really convenient.  Now we have a spare unit should this one ever go bad.  You get 20 brushes per full charge (10 days - 2x per day).  The first charge took about 24 hours, but after that it seems to charge fully in about 8 hours.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We both highly recommend this product.  The price seems a bit steep at first (compared to traditional brushes) but the clean you get is incomparable.  This toothbrush is a great investment in your health (you&#x27;d be surprised how many health issues are related to unhealthy teeth and gums) and smile.from (Daily Clean, Deep Clean, Sensitive, Whitening, and Massage) and even tells you when you&#x27;re brushing too hard.     <li> I have been a user of Braun electric toothbrushes for 20 years, ever since the first generation.  Except for the second generation, there are positive improvements in each generation of the product.  However, this latest generation has regressed.  I suspect that this is to save on production cost.  To me, the previous generation,  the Triumph model (Triumph Professional Care 9000) is the best of the lot and I wish I can still buy them.  The short-comings of this present model compared to the previous are    1) single voltage charger    The charger is now single voltage which means that I have to bring along a voltage transformer when I travel.  Who wants this?    2) long charging time    For the previous Triumph model, I can charge a completely drained toothbrush in about 12 hours.  Now it takes 24 hours.  This is a serious setback when I do not have time to charge the toothbrush, e.g. while traveling.    3) short battery life    My previous model which is a couple of years old can go for almost 2 weeks before it needs to be re-charged.  This model can last only about 8 days.  Again, this is a problem when you do not have access to power.    4) lack of proper display    Braun has removed the LCD display from this model.  Without the external Smart Guide, there is no way to tell how long have you been brushing your teeth.  Also, the pause, every 30 seconds, is long and is exceedingly irritating.  The long interruption disrupts smooth brushing of the teeth.    5) blinking LED while charging    Due to the absence of the LCD panel, the charging progress is indicated by blinking LED lights.  This is the method used by a previous generation of toothbrush.  After a while, the LED lights will wear out and stop blinking.  When this happens, there is no way to tell whether the toothbrush is charging and when it has a full charge.    I hope that Braun would take notice of these short-comings and bring back the previous generation of Trimph toothbrush.    +++++++++++++++++++Update - 1/31/2015    One and a half year later, the battery is now gone.  It would not hold the charge.  I spend 1 whole day charging it up and only get to use the toothbrush for 2 days before the battery is totally discharged.  Worse still, the red low charge light does not come on, so I am left with a mouthful of foam when the battery suddenly died.    Since I am rotating this toothbrush with my older Triumph which is still going strong, this means that the battery would have lasted less than 1 year if I am using this toothbrush exclusively.    I tried to open up the toothbrush to dispose of the battery, but the white cap at the bottom of the handle would not come off. I contacted the P&amp;G customer service and asked them how to remove the cap.  I was told to be a responsible consumer and dispose of the battery properly.  How am I suppose to be responsible when I cannot remove the battery?  This product really sucks.     <li> I&#x27;ve been using this brush for the better part of a month and for the most part, it&#x27;s identical to the [[ASIN:B004O76DEC Oral-B Professional Care SmartSeries 5000]] I purchased just over a year ago.  Overall, it does a great job cleaning your teeth.  For those of you using manual brushes that are considering moving up to electric, there is no contest - GET AN ELECTRIC BRUSH! Using your favorite toothpaste, The Oral-B will leave your mouth feeling very clean.  As with any toothbrush, manual or electric, it is still very important to floss daily.  When I floss at night, I notice is that there is less crud left between my teeth when using this brush with it&#x27;s Floss Action head..  Less, but not none, so DO continue to floss.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What I&#x27;m torn about is the \\&quot;nanny\\&quot; aspect of this Oral-B 5000 system and the external display.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There is a remote external display which stays in radio contact with the brush.  It displays a timer, along with a star and a bar for each of four sections of your mouth.  The four sections represented are the upper left, upper right, lower left and lower right sides of your mouth.  The brush has an internal timer synced with the external display and by default it emits a beep and it pauses every thirty seconds to signal that it&#x27;s time to move on to the next section.  The idea is to spend thirty seconds on each section for a total of two minutes of brushing time.  After two minutes at which time you&#x27;re done with all four sections, the brush beeps, pauses and a smiley face is displayed on the external display.  Oh, happy times!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;m torn about this system because I don&#x27;t need the timer and I don&#x27;t like the fact that you cannot turn it off.  I normally brush for over thirty seconds in each section (and I have my own way of brushing) and I don&#x27;t like the way the brush pauses to indicate that its time to move on.  Even though there are five \\&quot;modes of operation\\&quot; and one of them is 45 seconds per section (deep clean), you cannot set that mode as the default.  No, you have to press the mode button five times every time you brush in order to access that mode.  Since they go through all the trouble of the external display, why couldn&#x27;t they make it so you could choose and set your default options?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One useful aspect of the external display is that there is an indicator which lights up red when the brush detects that you are brushing too hard (if you&#x27;re putting too much pressure on the brush).  This is something I do appreciate as brushing too hard can really do a job on your gums (especially with a manual brush).  Its best to allow the brush head to do its job with light pressure.  Having the indicator, which seems fairly accurate, is nice.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One nitpick is that you pretty much have to keep the brush charging or it will be sluggish after two or three brushings.  The battery indicator is fairly useless as it will still show a full or 2/3 charge when the brush really needs to be charged to avoid it being sluggish.  The brush will still run, but it will be sluggish.  What I mean by sluggish is that the motor noticeably slows down from its peak output, so you&#x27;re not going to get the same clean.  The battery pack seems to be removable, but I cannot find a replacement.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Oral-B is one well made brush.  It&#x27;s made in Germany, and it feels solid and well-engineered.  It should last for years.  The Oral-B 5000 system has all the bells and whistles if you desire.  But if you can do without the external display, you could go with the less expensive [[ASIN:B008PEMBNC Oral-B Professional Precision 1000 Rechargeable Toothbrush]], which is basically the same brush, but without the external display.  It still has the internal 30 second timer which pauses after each section and five modes of operation.  It just does with out the external display and the indicator that lights up when you brush too hard.  If you can do without that, the 1000 is less than half the price for what is basically the same brush.nd timer which pauses after each section and five modes of operation.  It just does with out the external display and the indicator that lights up when you brush too hard.  If you can do without that, the 1000 is less than half the price for what is basically the same brush.</li>
    <li> Here are the reasons why I like it. I honestly can&#x27;t think of any cons...&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*The travel case is handy. Just take the toothbrush and your toothpaste and you&#x27;re all set. You don&#x27;t need to lug the stand since the toothbrush remains charged for several days.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*I like the red light that comes on when you&#x27;re brushing too hard. I had no idea that I was brushing too hard, so the warning light is great.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*The brush heads are interchangeable with other Oral-B toothbrushes, which is awesome! Since we now have 2 Oral-B toothbrushes it&#x27;s much easier to buy a set of replacement brush heads for BOTH, than it would be to have a different type for each toothbrush. I love this features since it saves both money and headaches (having a replacement head for 1 toothbrush when you really need a replacement head for the other toothbrush).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*The brush heads are changeable, meaning people who share the same bathroom can use the same toothbrush \\&quot;base\\&quot;, but change out the heads. This is a little skeevy for me, because I&#x27;d think there&#x27;s a bit of the other user&#x27;s toothpaste/saliva residue, but give it a good cleaning after each use, and you&#x27;re good. I&#x27;m not sure that I&#x27;ll use this feature, but it&#x27;s great to have instead of requiring people to buy multiple toothbrushes (which can get pricey quickly).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;*The little wireless monitor screen. I like it. Didn&#x27;t quite get it at first, but it also helps you to know when you&#x27;re brushing too hard and it helps you \\&quot;see\\&quot; the 30-second quadrants for the 4 areas of your mouth that make up the 2 minute drill. I think it&#x27;s a clock when not in use, but I haven&#x27;t been able to set the clock so far (and I stopped trying). You also don&#x27;t need it in order to travel with your toothbrush, which is nice. (You actually don&#x27;t need it at all, but I like it.)</li>
    <li> My husband and I bought this set from our dentist and we love it. It has space to store four different heads and has options for the type of cleaning you want. We bought an extra head for me. My husband normally hates power toothbrushes but he loves this one. And it helps make sure he brushes the right way. And the dentist is happy with both of us.</li>
    <li> Call me simple, but I love having the 30-second reminders to switch zones when I am brushing and the smiley face when you hit two minutes is a nice way to start the day. Like any electric toothbrush, the heads do wear a little quickly, but Amazon has pretty good deals on replacements.</li>
    <li> I received this toothbrush thru the Amazon Vine program, and reviewed it on the original product page. That page indicates it has been superseded (and therefore won&#x27;t link) by the one on this page, though they appear to be identical.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I started using a [[ASIN:B00240XRUY Oral-B Cross Action Power Toothbrush]] with the AAA battery about five years ago and the hygienist in my dentist&#x27;s office said there was a noticeable difference in the condition of my teeth and gums. When this one came along on Vine I thought, \\&quot;What a great way to upgrade.\\&quot; After using it a while I can say it was a worthwhile move.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As I take it out of the box, I notice it has a quality feel to it. I note it is made in Germany. It came with one \\&quot;Floss Action\\&quot; brush head.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So What&#x27;s to Like?&lt;br /&gt;The charging base can be kept separate from the brush head holder. If you are short on counter space, as I am, this is a handy feature. Mrs. Boilermate doesn&#x27;t care for any power brush, so the extra head holder is extraneous.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Easy to use. I think it is well balanced, and it fits my ham hand quite well. Use too much pressure, and the handle and monitor light up red. It easily rinses clean when I am done.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Of course it is louder than a manual brush, but it is quieter than the Cross Action. It has a smoother and more pleasant sound as well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Cross Action buzzes your teeth as it cleans. This one cleans without feeling like it&#x27;s going to vibrate your fillings out. The brush head feels softer but it feels like it is cleaning better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I like that the brush beeps and pauses briefly every 30 seconds as a reminder to move on to the next quadrant. It is designed so that you get used to brushing for the dentist recommended two minutes, but after the fourth quadrant it merely pauses and then continues running. It doesn&#x27;t shut off when you two minutes are up, a plus IMO.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The included monitor counts up the time while you brush and shows you which quadrant you have completed. It also shows which program you selected, and shows the time when you&#x27;re not using the toothbrush. The monitor may be useful if you have children and you&#x27;re trying to teach the proper way to brush the teeth. They may like the smiley face and the stars that light up as they complete each quadrant. The monitor can be stored on the shelf or mounted on the wall using a holder that supplied with the kit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The travel case makes it easy to take this when I travel.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What&#x27;s Not to Like?&lt;br /&gt;If you do need the extra heads, the holder takes up valuable counter space. It cannot be wall-mounted. Stored flat, the heads cannot drip dry as well, especially with the cover over them.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The replacement head cost. At over six bucks apiece, you could buy a whole new Cross Action brush for the cost of one refill head for this. And this kit only comes with one. If you have a family that uses this, the costs can add up very quickly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Next to Bottom Line&lt;br /&gt;Do we need this appliance? No. In the same sense we don&#x27;t need a power mower to mow the lawn. A push type reel mower will cut the grass but it really doesn&#x27;t do as good a job as a power mower. My dentist has told me for years that a power brush does a better job cleaning your teeth than a manual one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Bottom Line&lt;br /&gt;If it were my own money, would I buy the Oral B Professional 5000, or consider the [[ASIN:B003UKKHB4 Oral-B Professional 3000]] which has the same basic features but with fewer bells and whistles? If I had children I would probably consider this model. The visual guides on the monitor are good teaching aids. Since I don&#x27;t, and considering I would be the only one using it, I would probably save about 30 bucks and opt for the 3000.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;UPDATE 1/17/13&lt;br /&gt;I still really like this toothbrush, but...It turns out the monitor is a battery hog. I put two fresh alkaline batteries in the monitor when I received it in June of lastyear, and this week they are dead. Since the brush unit still works as before I don&#x27;t think I will bother to replace them. This only confirms my comments above...I don&#x27;t feel there is sufficient added value to justify the higher price this model commands over the Professional 3000.</li>

    <li> REVIEW UPDATE AFTER 3 WEEKS OF DAILY USE:&lt;br /&gt;This is an awesome product.  The \\&quot;timer\\&quot; function makes the time fly by.  I often want to continue after 2 minutes have passed.  My mouth feels cleaner than with any other toothbrush, and my teeth are noticeably whiter.&lt;br /&gt;The reasons why this product got 4 and not 5 stars are listed below in my original review.&lt;br /&gt;------------------------------------------------------------&lt;br /&gt;ORIGINAL REVIEW (after several days of use)&lt;br /&gt;------------------------------------------------------------&lt;br /&gt;I enjoy using this product, and it appears to be extremely well made.  I have two problems with this purchase right off the bat:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1.This is a \\&quot;Braun\\&quot; electric toothbrush.  I don&#x27;t know if Oral-b had it made special or if it is a off-the-shelf product for Braun.  I  bought this toothbrush because I trust the Oral-b brand.  All the parts (toothbrush, wireless guide, recharge base, etc.) are branded \\&quot;Braun\\&quot;.  Some also say \\&quot;Oral-b\\&quot; in smaller letters.  The only thing that is made by \\&quot;Oral-b\\&quot; is the single brush head that came in the package.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2. It is not a \\&quot;retail\\&quot; package.  If you buy this toothbrush in a store, it comes in a box with a lot of info on it.  What I received was a small brown cardboard carton with the toothbrush and accessories packed inside.  I now see that Amazon lists the packaging as \\&quot;Amazon Frustration Free\\&quot;.  It turns out \\&quot;Amazon Frustration Free\\&quot; means a much less fancy package.  Kudos to Amazon for reducing packaging waste (and shipping costs), but I would have been happier if I had known to expect this.</li>

    <li> I was looking to replace my Sonicare (low end Essence) brush. My dentist suggested and had a great deal on an Oral B Professional Precision 5000. Overall if you are trying to decide between the Oral B Professional 5000 and a Sonicare brush I would whole heartedly suggest going with Oral B - it&#x27;s a much more complete and cost effectivesystem.    UPDATE: After using my toothbrush for 1.5 years it stopped working, but Braun offers a 2 year warranty for this product! If you need to contact warranty support, call do not email. Automatic battery cut off when fully charged is a plus. Even shuts the lights off of the unit to limit electric draw. I do find that the pressure sensor to protect your gums is set way off. To set off the warning you&#x27;d have to purposefully be trying to sand off your gums. Overall a 4 because I still feel like it could be faster motion or more of a sonic motion. The pulsations seem pretty well set.</li>

It happens to have a toothbrush on the end, because that is what people are used to putting in their mouth.  But the main point seems to be to apply ultrasonic cleaning to your teeth, like your jeweler uses on old jewelry.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In contrast, the Oral-B seems to be more designed to actually gets its bristles into spaces, and to massage your gums.  More motion, but less intense.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now, regarding the 5000 versus other Oral-B models.  Like others, I find a lot of the included accessories largely unnecessary. More importantly, these days we already have too many wireless devices that start interfering with each other.  Wifi, Dish Network remotes, Senn 180 wireless headphones and Logitech M510 mouse are all important to me, but adding anything more is a dubious proposition - especially if it is unnecessary.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, while I have not used the simpler models in the Oral-B \\&quot;Professional\\&quot; line, I would recommend that you consider those, especially since they look like a much better dollar value.</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve been using the [[ASIN:B008UKTJSG Braun Triumph Professional Care 9900 Power Toothbrush with Smart Guide]] for about four years, after finishing up some extensive dental restoration. On the plus side, the Precision 5000 brush actually lights up when you&#x27;re applying too much pressure. The Triumph series only blinked a recessed light on the LCD.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One big, wonderful design change is the holder for the individual brushes. On the Triumph series, moisture would collect at the base, and it would get gross without regular cleaning. This holder is a much simpler design that prevents accumulation, and that&#x27;s way easier to clean.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Speaking of cleaning... if you use any sort of restorative toothpaste (e.g. [[ASIN:B004TL900M Sensodyne Pronamel]]) you absolutely MUST make sure that the motor is clean after each use. In any case, the absence of drilling and scraping since Oral-B Professional products came in to my life makes this one of those rare unintentionally life-changing products.n changes, Oral-B has got away from the massive Braun plug that they used on previous models (and still use on Braun shavers) and instead uses a normal North American plug.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All things being equal, there&#x27;s usually some sort of rebate going on high-end Oral-B products, and if you can pick this up for less than a Benjamin, you&#x27;d do well to get in on that deal.     <li> I&#x27;ve been using this toothbrush for about two years now and have enjoyed it. I think it does a wonderful job of keeping your teeth clean. They charge a stiff price for the toothbrush (lets face it, they aren&#x27;t cheap by any means) and expensive replacement heads. They design it with a soldered battery that prevents the consumer from replacing it themselves, ensuring that you either purchase another one or send it off to them for battery replacement. Capitalism at it&#x27;s finest.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The product itself is sound, but just be aware that you&#x27;re purchasing something with a battery that will eventually fail. You will not be able to replace it with ease or without a soldering kit. It will either need repaired or repurchased.</li>

    <li> I do like this new toothbrush from Oral-B. (Also the heads and chargers are interchangeable, that is a great bonus).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While you get the same basic electric brush, the question was whether the small improvements make up for the price difference, and the answer is a definite yes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1 - The receiver with the smiley face&lt;br /&gt;The first difference is the addition of the remote receiver. Here you can choose the strength and the time of brushing among different options. This is a definite plus&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3 - Head storage&lt;br /&gt;Electric brush maintenance and cleaning is important. Since they all stay in vertical position, the remaining \\&quot;gunk\\&quot; flows down, and builds up on the handle, and other places. It is better to get the head out from time to time, and clean up everything.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The addition of the integrated head storage near the base is a real convenience. Now, each time I brush my teeth, I take thehead off, and then wash everything.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And, since there are four slots, depending on your preference, you might choose to share a single base among your family. Again it is just an option, and depends on your choice.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4 - Refinements&lt;br /&gt;While the older models already have the essentials, this new brush clearly improves upon them. For example, the pressure warning (when you press the brush too much upon your teeth), now has a red light element as well. The 30 seconds and 2 minutes marks are now more definite, and there is an additional audio beep. The brush itself feels more sturdy, and so on.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall if you are looking for a long term investment on your teeth (and you should, since they will hopefully be with you you entire life), I could recommend this product. If you looking for a budget one [[ASIN:B003UKM9CO Precision 1000]] would be an alternative.</li>

    <li> Oral-B Professional Healthy Clean + Floss Action Precision 5000 Rechargeable Electric Toothbrush&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I purchased a Precision 5000 earlier in the year, and this Precision 5000 is quite different. First, the packaging has been improved - it is now similar to Amazon&#x27;s Frustration-Free packaging and most likely better for the environment due to less plastics.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The new Precision 5000 has an updated SmartGuide that uses stars to indicate which quadrant you&#x27;re brushing (or supposed to be brushing) along with a smiley face that is always on with the clock. The charging base and base of the 5000 is different -it now resembles the traditional Oral B base where the charger has a nub that clips into a recess on the toothbrush. The 5000 I purchased earlier in the year was also inductive, but the entire base of the brush just sits into a ring to charge.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The new 5000 also uses an audible beep every 30 seconds along with Oral B&#x27;s traditional pause. However, for each 30 second interval, there is an extra beep. So at the end of a 2 minute brushing session, there will be 4 consecutive beeps which can get annoying.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The brush head interface remains the same, so the existing inventory of brush heads will work on this model.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There&#x27;s still no way to set it to default to sensitive mode. Oral B now requires you to do an extra press of the mode button to get into the sensitive/feather mode (2 total) versus 1 with the older 5000.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall: 5/5 stars, still the same great Precision 5000 but with some minor tweaks.     <li> I&#x27;ve owned a number of electric toothbrushes and the only two brands that are worth anything are Oral-B and Phillips.     <li> I have been using an Oral-B electric toothbrush for the past four years and regret I did not switch over many years before. My teeth definitely feel cleaner after a two minute session. The SmartSeries 5000 is a step up from various Oral-B models I have used in the past. The basic speed for a daily clean seems to be the same. Oral-B uses standard heads and chargers throughout their product line so this makes all my old accessories compatible -- a good thing. A good manual (written in clear English) is included along with the brush and accessories (with the former... gasp... actually being made in Germany.) A two year warranty (good) and a 60 day money back guarantee are included.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This model comes with a charger, one head, a traveling case and a separate wireless smart guide unit. The cleaning modes for the brush are Daily Clean, Deep Clean, Sensitive, Whitening, and Massage. I am sure all these modes are fine, but 98 percent of the time I use \\&quot;Daily Clean.\\&quot; The SmartGuide takes some explaining. This is a small wireless device (comes with optional wall mount and 2 AA batteries) that is basically a timer for your brush cycles.  When you activate your toothbrush it sends a signal to the SmartGuide and shows how long you have been brushing your teeth and with the use of multiple icons how well you have been doing.  If you are using too much pressure, a red light appears on both the brush and the guide display -- I found that I was brushing hard way too often so this has been a helpful feature for me. Not sure if harder brushing actually hurts my oral health, but definitely makes the brush heads wear out faster. The SmartGuide works as a normal digital clock for your bathroom.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The brush automatically beeps (in the daily clean cycle) every 30 seconds to indicate when the recommended two minute brushing time is complete and the SmartGuide has a large quadrant icon showing the stages of brushing. I laughed when I saw the device and thought it was gimmicky, but now I am hooked and watch the screen. The toothbrush also has its own battery indicator (3 levels) -- most other models only indicate if the battery needs to be charged (like immediately!). I am getting about 10 days of use (2x/day&#x3D;20 brushings) as described -- though I expect that to diminish as the unit ages as rechargeable batteries aren&#x27;t good forever (and are NOT replaceable despite the fact they are removable.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A middle-of-the-road Oral-B toothbrush is probably fine for most folks, but if you catch this model on sale or with a rebate it should be a brush that your dentist is happy about you using. I find my replacement heads cheapest at the local warehouse store that starts with the letter C. My hygienist never complains about my teeth (in fact I have no cavities period) but gum issues do run in my family -- hopefully with a good oral health plan including this brush I won&#x27;t have to suffer the same fate as my parents.</li>

    <li> This Oral-B Professional Healthy Clean Precision 5000 Electric Toothbrush is an updated version of the Oral-B SmartSeries 5000 Toothbrush.  I own both toothbrushes, and here are the differences between the two:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The biggest change is with the on-handle display.  The old version had a small display which showed the charge level, in 4 different increments.  When the battery was low, the last bar on the screen would blink.  You could see the charge level at all times also.  With the new version, the display is gone, and has been replaced by LED lights (in 3 different increments).  The light is green when charged, and flashes red when the battery is low.  One annoying thing about the new version is the LED light turns off when not brushing.  So you can only see the charge level while the toothbrush is in use.  I prefer the old method where you can see the charge level at all times.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The charging cradle has been slightly improved.  The old version had a ring base that the toothbrush fit into.  The new one has a smaller base that the toothbrush is placed on.  Not a huge improvement, but I like the new one better because it doesn&#x27;t get your bathroom counter dirty with toothpaste residue.  Now you just need to clean the base.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The 30 second notification to move to the next quadrant has changed.  Now, there is more of a noticeable stop after each 30 seconds (though it&#x27;s just a split second).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;- The SmartTimer now has a star system that rates you on your brushing time.  If you go the full two minutes, all four stars will darken (and the smiley face on the display smiles).  If you skip out on the time, not all the stars will darken and you won&#x27;t see the smiley face.  This isn&#x27;t a big deal to me, but may provide positive reinforcement for those who find it hard to go the full 2 minutes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So as you can see, the changes overall are pretty small.  If you have a SmartSeries 5000, you probably don&#x27;t need to upgrade to the new Precision 5000.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, the toothbrush performance is still stellar.  It provides 5 cleaning modes- daily clean, deep clean, sensitive, whitening, and massage.  You also have a variety of tooth brush heads to use.  I prefer the Floss Action, but my wife uses the Sensitive one.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One thing I have noticed is that you have to be careful with what type of toothpaste to use.  Some pastes create a lot more liquid than others while brushing, and you may find it tough to go a full 2 minutes without taking a break to spit it out.  I had to do trial and error with a few different brands to see which one I liked (Colgate Total seems to work well).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My dentist has seen improvement with these toothbrushes vs. the old SonicCare I used.  That is reason enough for me to splurge on these types of toothbrushes.recision 5000.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, the toothbrush performance is still stellar.     <li> The headline says it all. I bought this product only because it was the fanciest looking and most expensive one of electric brushes I could find.     <li> I have been using and enjoying an Oral-B Triumph toothbrush for several years; which worked flawlessly until recently.  The charging capacity suddenly started dropping drastically, to where I would have to charge it about once every 2 days.  I was offered the ability to test and review this new Oral-B Healthy Clean + Floss Precision 5000 toothbrush, which I gratefully accepted.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Unboxing the new product, and now after using it for the past month, I can honestly say that it is extremely similar to my previous Triumph model Oral-B device.  Size and weight are about the same.  It is just as noisy as my previous toothbrush as well.  My old Triumph handle had an LCD display, to show battery level and charging status.  This new handle uses LED lighting instead, which only lights up when the handle is powered on and for a few seconds after being powered off.  The Floss Action brush heads haven&#x27;t changed , but I do like the selection of 5 cleaning modes (regular clean, deep clean, sensitive, whitening, and massage).  I was discouraged to see that Oral-B didn&#x27;t include the variety of head attachments that they did with my previous model.  The new Precision 5000 only came with a single Floss Action head, while my Triumph came with the same Floss Action head, and added a Sensitive head, a Power Tip head, Pro White head, and some kind of tongue cleaner head.  Then again, considering the substantially lower cost of this new Precision 5000 model, compared to my high priced Triumph 9900 from 5 or more years ago, I guess I can see why they left out a few of the extra frills.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The new Smart Guide display is cute and informative, but I do not find it extremely useful.  It lights up one star for every 30 seconds you brush, and the goal is to light up 4-stars to indicate you have brushed for the recommended 2 minutes.  You are even presented with a big smiley face, to give you that extra sense of pride in what you have accomplished.  It will provide you with a bonus star (5-stars in all) if you brush for an additional 30 seconds or more.  The best part is, if you brush long enough to get that extra bonus star, you will sometimes (not every time) be greeted with a winking smiley face.  Now who wouldn&#x27;t like that?  The Smart Guide also shows you what brushing mode you are using, displays an icon to show you when it is time to replace your brush head, and also has a red (might be dark orange) lighted indicator to warn if you are pressing against your teeth too hard with the brush.  There is a rather large LED light on the back of the powered brush handle as well, which flashes brightly if you are applying too much pressure when brushing.  I really like the light on the handle, as it prevents the need for the user to keep watching the Smart Guide display (which can sometimes be difficult to see from a distance).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Precision 5000 series toothbrush, like all other Oral-B powered brushes I have used, does a splendid job of cleaning my teeth.  My dentist has had nothing but good things to say about my teeth and gums since I started using my Oral-B Triumph several years ago.  It provides a comfortable and stimulating scrubbing action to your teeth and gum-line, but isn&#x27;t overly aggressive to cause discomfort.  This scrubbing action does a great job of removing plaque, preventing stains, and the Floss Action heads do well at getting between teeth and removing food particles.  The Oral-B Precision 5000 is far from being whisper quiet, so be prepared for a little noise once you switch it on.  It is also a little bulky, and has s fair amount of weight to it.  I don&#x27;t find it to be clumsy or heavy at all, and enjoy the solid feel of the handle overall.  The handle is waterproof, and has a good rubbery grip surface.  My only real complaint about the new Precision 5000 series toothbrush is the pause in brushing every 30 seconds.  While I understand the concept behind the physical feedback, to let you know it&#x27;s time to switch quadrants in your mouth, and that the physical feedback eliminates the need to watch the LCD display for visual indicators, I don&#x27;t appreciate the interruption in the brushing motion.  In fact, every 30 seconds the pause gets longer, so that you can hear this faint little beep that grows in number during each pause.  So, after the first thirty seconds you get a very short pause, with a single beep.  After another 30 seconds you get a pause twice as long, with two beeps.  By the time you get to the fourth pause, it is so long that you just stand there looking at yourself awkwardly in the mirror, waiting for the stupid thing to start brushing again.  The engineer that came up with this concept should be slapped silly, in my honest opinion!  My wife has a Sonicare toothbrush that provides a really short stutter in brushing action every 30 seconds, which doesn&#x27;t interrupt the brushing process, but provides enough feedback to alert the user that another 30 seconds has passed.  I think Braun (Oral-B) needs to hire the engineer from Sonicare, to redesign their feedback system, which would bring this device closer to being a 5-star product.  As it is now, I consider the Oral-B Precision 5000 power toothbrush to be a solid 4 to 4 and  star product.  It does a great job cleaning my teeth, and I have very few complaints about its style, build quality, or feature set.  Cleaning our teeth should be treated as a vital element of one&#x27;s daily personal hygiene regimen, and I highly recommend the [[ASIN:B008PEMOV6 Oral-B Professional Healthy Clean + Floss Action Precision 5000 Rechargeable Electric Toothbrush]] as the right tool for the job.rants in your mouth, and that the physical feedback eliminates the need to watch the LCD display for visual indicators, I don&#x27;t appreciate the interruption in the brushing motion. So, after the first thirty seconds you get a very short pause, with a single beep.  After another 30 seconds you get a pause twice as long, with two beeps.
